Current Commentary

Sun Yat-sen's Birthday During National Crisis and the Fourth National Congress

Today is the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's birth. The Kuomintang's Fourth National Congress in Nanjing also officially opens today. Holding such an important meeting on a day of great and glorious commemoration further highlights its significance. At the same time, the nation faces a multitude of crises. The people are drowning in floods, the country is threatened by powerful enemies, the situation is precarious, and crises are emerging all around. The opening of the Fourth National Congress today further highlights the enormous difficulty of its responsibilities.

What we find regrettable today is that the Chinese Kuomintang, founded by Sun Yat-sen, has failed to maintain solid unity and consistent action in recent years. Even today, Nanjing and Guangdong are still holding their respective Fourth National Congresses. This is truly an unfortunate phenomenon. However, if both sides can hold their meetings and truly cooperate, and if, after the meetings, both sides sincerely work together for permanent unity, then the temporary shadow will not detract from the brightness of the sun. This would be a great blessing not only for the future of the Kuomintang but also something on which the future of our nation deeply relies.

We are experiencing national difficulties and our hearts are filled with worry. After silently observing the situation, we respectfully submit several points for the Congress's consideration.

First, Dr. Sun Yat-sen dedicated himself to revolution for forty years, accumulating his experience and knowledge. He personally formulated the Three Principles of the People and the Founding Strategies. The depth of his theory and the breadth of his insights are truly the key to saving China. Since Dr. Sun Yat-sen's death, the responsibility for promoting and developing the Three Principles of the People and realizing the Founding Strategies lies entirely with those who adhere to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, that is, with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's only legacy, the Chinese Kuomintang. In various countries around the world, the thoughts and propositions of revolutionary leaders during their lifetimes are mostly studied, explained, and developed by their disciples and followers after their deaths. However, since Dr. Sun Yat-sen's death and the Kuomintang's unification of the country, followers of Sun Yat-senism have been diligently engaged in politics, and very few people have paid attention to the work of organizing and clarifying Sun Yat-senism. The division of leaders and internal party disputes over the years, as well as the obscuring of the principles, are the main causes of this. Therefore, from now on, those who adhere to Sun Yat-senism and the members of the Chinese Kuomintang who practice the Three Principles of the People should, at least some of them, shift their enthusiasm from politics to the study of the Three Principles of the People in order to clarify the principles, unify the theory, and complete Dr. Sun Yat-sen's unfinished legacy.

Second, revolutionary party members should only have sacrifice and absolutely no enjoyment of happiness. If there is any, it should be on the day of the revolution's success, after all the people have obtained happiness. People who have traveled to the Soviet Union have praised the Bolshevik Party members for their hardship. Party members, as individuals, have almost no rights to speak of, and this spirit is extremely admirable. Today, the revolution of the Three Principles of the People has not yet succeeded, and the people's suffering has not yet been alleviated. However, the rights and comforts enjoyed by Kuomintang members may exceed those of the people. The ruling party bears a difficult responsibility. "The revolution has not yet succeeded, and party members still need to work hard." Enjoying rights is not yet the time. To worry before the people worry and to rejoice after the people rejoice is to be truly worthy of a revolutionary party member. Therefore, this Fourth National Congress should pay attention to correcting the mentality of party members seeking comfort and encourage their spirit of struggle in order to promote the National Revolution and bring it to an early success.

Third, the principles and policies of a political party, if it wants to win the sympathy and support of the broad masses, should not rely on empty slogans, but on the demonstration of facts. What the people demand are real and concrete facts, not empty promises. Before this Fourth National Congress, the Kuomintang has already held three representative congresses. Let's not talk about the first two. Even the resolutions of the Third Congress have accumulated into a huge volume. Plans have been determined for both domestic affairs and foreign relations. However, if we examine them today, have they all been implemented? Gathering the elite of the entire party, we are not worried about the lack of resolutions, but about the inability to implement the resolutions. It is better to take action than to sit and talk. The Kuomintang after taking power should pay even more attention to this. Therefore, this Congress should strictly review past achievements and, even more importantly, mobilize all party members to strive for the realization of the resolutions of this Congress.

Fourth, the country is currently facing unprecedented difficulties. Disaster relief for floods, recovery of vitality, recovery of lost territories in the Northeast, and resistance to violent and powerful neighbors all urgently require our government to lead the people in joint efforts. What's more, earlier, world figures speculated that the outbreak of World War II would either be in the Far East or in Western Europe, and their views were not consistent. Since the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, world opinion has unanimously determined that the Far East issue is the powder keg for a second war and is unavoidable. Our country is the center of the Far East issue. If a major war unfortunately breaks out one day and our country has no way to fight, then the country's future will be unimaginable. Therefore, the most important mission of this Congress is how to overcome the current national crisis and how to deal with the future international situation. There should be comprehensive plans for both domestic and foreign affairs, so that we can stabilize our country amidst the turmoil.

Domestic Important Telegrams II

League of Nations Secretary-General's Representative to Visit Japan to Inquire About True Intentions

(Tokyo) Walter, an official from the Secretariat of the League of Nations in China, will travel from Shanghai to Tokyo as a special envoy of Secretary-General Drummond. He is expected to arrive in Tokyo on the 12th. The purpose of Walter's trip is to meet with Japanese Foreign Minister Shidehara and inquire about Japan's true intentions in order to find a way for the League of Nations to resolve the situation. The public is paying close attention to the results of this meeting. (Jiji News Agency telegram, 11th)

Japan Reinforces Troops in Eastern Provinces; Four Japanese Warships Head to Lushun

(Tokyo) Japan is currently sending a division of troops to Manchuria as reinforcements, scheduled to depart on the 15th. (Guomin News Agency telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) The return of the Korean Army to its original unit and the dispatch of divisions from mainland Japan to Manchuria were announced by the Ministry of the Army this afternoon. (Jiji News Agency telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) The Naval Minister, who was with the Emperor in Kyushu for naval exercises, is now returning to Tokyo due to the possible developments in the North China situation. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) Four destroyers are currently sailing from the Wu naval port to Lushun, and one cruiser from Sasebo is heading to Yokosuka today to await orders. This movement of warships is reportedly due to the increasingly serious situation in North China. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has received an official report this evening regarding the riots in Tianjin, stating that this is purely a conflict between Chinese people and that Japanese soldiers are not involved. However, military authorities have already made preparations for security to protect the Japanese concession. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) A mixed brigade of the Eighth Division stationed in the northern part of Japan has now been approved by the Emperor to be transferred to Manchuria. Departure orders have been issued today. The brigade will replace the mixed brigade that went to Manchuria from Korea on September 19th. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

Japan to Further Propose Joint Control of China; Japanese Officials' Absurd Arguments; Cabinet Resolves to Stand Firm

(Tokyo) The attitude Japan should take when the League of Nations Administrative Council reconvenes on October 16 to discuss the Manchurian Incident has been clarified today. Officials stated that Japan will not make any concessions or slightly alter the five basic principles it proposed during the previous council meeting as the basis for a solution, which must be acknowledged by China. Japan will also further make the Administrative Council understand that only foreigners can give China a faithful government and plan a method for foreigners to manage China, so as to guarantee peace and order, good administration, and the necessity of respecting treaties. Japanese public opinion is mostly pessimistic about the outcome of the League of Nations meeting. However, officials seem to believe that if the League of Nations does not act hastily, then the outlook for Japan will not be bad. According to the opinion of today's spokesperson for the officials, Japan initially assumed that the world already knew that China's national policy was to abolish or disregard its so-called unequal treaties. Now, it realizes that this assumption was a mistake and will work to correct the previous error. The method is not to explain its own behavior but to focus on explaining the past history of the dispute, so that the League of Nations will understand the necessity of a fundamental solution. Japan will submit to the League of Nations a list of China's violations of treaty rights and strive to make the League of Nations understand that to have a faithful government in China, there must be some form of foreign intervention. If the League of Nations agrees with Japan's view and China truly has the sincerity to trust the League of Nations, then China should immediately agree to this plan. Japanese officials also said that the Manchurian problem is a matter of life and death for Japan and will never change its previously proposed demands. The rumors that Japan will comply with the scope when the League of Nations Administrative Council reconvenes are not true. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government held a cabinet meeting today to discuss how to deal with the League of Nations Council meeting in Paris on the 16th. After careful consultation, the following policy was decided:

Regardless of the attitude the League of Nations takes in the future, Japan will absolutely not withdraw its troops until security in Manchuria is safely maintained. (Jiji News Agency telegram, 11th)

(Tokyo) This afternoon, a National Assembly on the External Situation was held in Shiba Park, with over 8,000 people attending. A declaration of a firm foreign policy was resolved, and it was decided to send representatives to deliver this resolution to the Prime Minister, various ministers, and diplomats from League of Nations member states. (Jiji News Agency telegram, 11th)

Stimson Plans to Devise a Plan, Hoping to End the Sino-Japanese Dispute After Implementation

(Washington) Officials in the US government are very concerned about the constant reports of minor conflicts between Chinese and Japanese troops in the Three Northeastern Provinces, as well as the tense situation in Tianjin, where order has not yet been fully restored. It has recently been confirmed that Stimson has indeed drafted a plan, hoping to end the Sino-Japanese dispute after its implementation. However, its nature remains strictly confidential, and what kind of action will be taken has not been revealed. Today, the State Department received a report from the US Consul in Tianjin that the people in the British and French concessions in Tianjin are very unstable. It is reported that the property of American nationals in the two concessions is worth as much as ten million US dollars, so officials in the US government are quite concerned. In addition, a report was received that after General Ma Zhanshan rejected the Japanese request to withdraw troops to ten kilometers north of Jiangqiao, there were battles along the Tao'an Road. (Guomin News Agency telegram, 10th)

New British Foreign Secretary's Attendance at League of Nations Should Make Significant Contributions; US Government Sends Dawes to Attend

(Geneva) The League of Nations is extremely pleased to hear that the new British Foreign Secretary, Sir John Simon, will personally attend the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting on November 16. It is widely believed that Simon, with his strong capabilities and the prestige of the new British National Government backing him, will be able to join French Prime Minister Briand in making significant contributions to silence the alarm bells that have been ringing here for days. When the Administrative Council meets on the 16th, the United States has been notified. Speakers say that the US Ambassador to France is not currently in Paris, so US Ambassador to the UK Dawes may attend the meeting. This statement has not yet been confirmed, but there is no doubt that US observer Gilbert will attend. (Reuters telegram, 10th)

(Washington) The State Department today ordered US Ambassador to the UK General Dawes to represent the United States at the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting to be held in Paris on November 16. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

British Foreign Secretary Sir John Simon told Ransbury in the Lower House today that he intends to go to Paris to attend the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting. The Council has the famous Briand as Chairman, and with the moral assistance of the United States, it should be able to resolve the unfortunate Manchurian Incident. The Administrative Council has tried to find common ground between the two sides in order to seek a binding resolution. Unfortunately, it has not been completely successful. If there is no unanimous agreement, then the resolution passed has no binding force in law. Sir John Simon also said that since the Administrative Council adjourned, it has continued to try to promote coordination. When the Administrative Council reconvenes, it will carefully continue this effort. He heard that some Japanese troops have withdrawn to the South Manchuria Railway area, but there are battles again in northwestern Manchuria. As for the riots in Tianjin, their meaning is unclear. When the Foreign Secretary announced that he would personally attend the Administrative Council meeting, the entire House cheered. Labor Party MP Thorn asked what the real cause of the Manchurian Incident was, but Sir John Simon refused to answer. He also said that Britain has not sent reinforcements to China. Labor Party MP Griffith asked whether the Foreign Secretary was going to Paris with his usual spirit of peace, and the Foreign Secretary smiled and nodded. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

The Manchurian problem was mentioned in both Houses of Parliament in London today when discussing the British King's Speech. Former Minister of Public Works Lansbury, who is now the leader of the opposition party, declared in the Lower House that both China and Japan are members of the League of Nations, so the British government should clearly inform the Lower House of the measures it has proposed with other countries to end the dispute and avoid further bloodshed. Prime Minister MacDonald did not criticize the Manchurian Incident in his reply but said that he would announce the latest news about the matter tomorrow. Lord Knollys spoke in the Upper House, welcoming the British King's concern for the work of the League of Nations and saying that the League of Nations is currently encountering the most difficult event in its history in its efforts to prevent a major upheaval in the Far East. He hoped that war could be avoided, but if this goal could not be achieved, he hoped that the League of Nations could limit the adverse effects of future events. (Reuters telegram, 11th)

Debuchi Explains Attitude Towards China to US Government

(Washington) Japanese Ambassador Debuchi today reiterated to the US government his attitude towards China's diplomacy, which has been adopted and must be maintained. This morning, the Japanese ambassador told US Secretary of State Stimson that Japan insists on withdrawing troops only after the safety of Japanese lives and property is guaranteed and normal relations between China and Japan have been restored. The Japanese government may not insist on the final concrete resolution of the 300 outstanding cases between China and Japan, but it requires China to respect the existing treaties regarding the Three Northeastern Provinces. Japanese troops are currently guarding the Nen River Bridge but are not advancing or endangering the Chinese Eastern Railway. (Reuters telegram, 10th)

Japan to Reassign Representative to League of Nations

(Nanjing) A telegram from Tokyo on the 11th said that the Japanese government is considering reassigning the Japanese representative to the League of Nations Administrative Council, either Ambassador Yoshida to Italy or Ambassador Matsudaira to the UK. Japan is now planning to organize a large-scale propaganda machine internationally and intends to use the French Paris News to oppose China. (Central News Agency telegram, 11th)

Japanese in Geneva Pay Attention to Propaganda; Bottles with Anti-Propaganda Items Thrown into Shi Zhaoji's Office

(Geneva) A new development in Manchurian propaganda has been discovered in Geneva today, and the police are now paying attention to it. For weeks, reports of propaganda and counter-propaganda, rebuttals and refutations, have been incessant. But today, extremists have taken a hand, and the methods they are using are completely beyond the scope of ordinary diplomacy. Someone threw a bottle containing a protest against British imperialism's aid to Chiang Kai-shek through the window of the office of Dr. Shi Zhaoji, the Chinese chief representative. Another bottle, containing the same document, apparently intended for the British consulate, was abandoned in front of a neighboring house. No one saw who threw these bottles, but the police are now investigating. (Reuters telegram, 10th)

Meeting of Japanese Residents' Association in Shandong Province Sends Telegram to Briand for Counter-Propaganda

(Qingdao) Japanese residents held a meeting at the Residents' Association at noon on the 11th and resolved to send a telegram to League of Nations member Briand in the name of the Shandong Residents' Association, saying that I have not fulfilled various outstanding issues in Shandong, and demanding participation rights in municipal administration, making various counter-propaganda, and telegraphing Arawata to prepare a proposal. (Special telegram, 11th)

(Jinan) The Japanese Shandong Residents' Association today telegraphed Arawata, requesting that the following be submitted to the League of Nations: 1. China has not yet fulfilled the Sino-Japanese agreement on resolving the Shandong issue in 1922. 2. The right of Japanese people to participate in Qingdao's municipal administration, stipulated in the treaty, has also not been realized. 3. It is regrettable that the common interests of China and Japan cannot be realized. (Special telegram, 11th)

All-Manchuria Japanese Congress Meeting Advanced in Shenyang

(Harbin) The All-Manchuria Japanese Congress was brought forward to the 7th in Shenyang. It was resolved: (1) to request the authorities to increase troops to absolutely maintain security; (2) to study the matter of economic turnaround; (3) to earnestly request the resolution of various outstanding Sino-Japanese issues; (4) in this situation, to request relief for the poor. Since the Japanese army occupied the Northeast, the business of Japanese nationals has plummeted, and many do not want the military to persist in this way for long. (Special telegram, 10th)

Various Groups in Harbin Send Personnel to Heilongjiang to Comfort Troops

(Harbin) Groups in Harbin are enthusiastically taking money to Heilongjiang to comfort the troops. Seven groups have already sent personnel to the front to deliver supplies. (Special telegram, 11th)

Purpose of Japanese Aiding Bandits

(Beiping) A certain foreigner talked about the Japanese side's purpose in luring bandits: (1) to use bandits to disturb Chinese troops, hoping to drive out the Chinese troops and administrative agencies east of Yuguan, in order to achieve their attempt to support Manchurian independence; (2) to lead bandits to Shenyang to plunder, in order to cover up the Japanese army's plundering in Shenyang and avoid liability for compensation. (Special telegram, 11th)

Japanese Embassy Convenes Meeting of Residents

(Beiping) The Japanese Embassy convened a meeting of residents last night, which did not end until after 10 o'clock. The content of the meeting was very secret and could not be found out. Japanese residents in Qinhuangdao were ordered to withdraw on the 10th, and most have already returned to their country by ship. (Special telegram, 11th)

Japanese Warships Continue to Arrive in Hankou; Japanese Residents in Qinhuangdao Ordered to Withdraw

(Hankou) The Japanese warship "Yanagi" arrived in Hankou on the 11th. The "Seso", "Dotrito", and "Chirigen" warships will arrive in Hankou within five days. It is reported that Japanese naval commander Shiozawa has informed Japanese residents that if Japanese goods are inspected, they should be taken back by force. (Special telegram, 11th)

(Hankou) Police Chief of Staff Ye Peng admonished officers and soldiers at a security conference: 1. Protect Japanese residents and their businesses. If an accident occurs, the responsible officials will be severely punished. 2. Strictly arrest hooligans and local ruffians who are instigated to make trouble, and those who are caught will be executed on the spot. 3. Police stations along the Japanese border and those adjacent to the Japanese border should deploy multiple layers of guard posts on Chinese streets 50 or 100 meters away from the Japanese border to prevent any incidents. Finally, he declared that all security officers and soldiers should use their bones as city walls and their blood as moats, and defend our territory with legitimate means and prevent any violent aggression. (Special telegram, 11th)

Chiang Holds a Banquet to Entertain Representatives from Northeast Petition; Petition Delegation Petitions the Central Party Headquarters; Zhang Ji and Wu Tiecheng Answer Everything

(Nanjing) Chiang met with the Northeast people's petition delegation at the military academy at 4 pm on the 11th. First, representatives Feng Yong and others stated that the country is facing a national crisis, and they unanimously hoped for domestic peace and unity to unite against foreign aggression. Chiang expressed full acceptance and gave them words of encouragement. Chiang hosted a banquet at the Lichi Society tonight at 8 pm, inviting a total of 70 representatives. Chiang gave a speech, expressing his welcome, and the banquet ended at 10 pm. (Special telegram, 11th)

(Nanjing) A delegation of more than 600 people from the Northeast People's National Salvation Petition, led by Feng Yong, petitioned the Central Party Headquarters at noon on the 11th. 1. Announce the process of the Shanghai Peace Conference. 2. Explain the meaning of the separate Fourth National Congresses. 3. Complete unification immediately. 4. Recover the lost territories in the Northeast by a set date. 5. If the violent Japanese continue to invade various places, they should be stopped by force. 6. Prepare to declare war on Japan. 7. Offer rewards for the arrest of pro-Japanese traitors Yuan Jinkai, Xi Qia, Zhang Haipeng, etc. 8. How should the officials responsible for the lost territories be punished? Central Committee members Zhang Ji and Wu Tiecheng met with the representatives. Zhang Ji first gave a speech, saying that Japan's invasion of our eastern provinces this time is aimed at destroying our China, so the fall of the Northeast is the fall of China. The Central Government has made a great determination and vowed to recover the lost territories in the Northeast. Currently, all countries are dissatisfied with Japan's atrocities and will be able to uphold justice and impose sanctions. The people of the Northeast have a glorious history of the past several thousand years, and you are the excellent youths of the Northeast, who can lead the people of the Northeast to unite and fight together under the leadership of the Central Government to recover the lost territories and save China. Wu Tiecheng then gave a speech, saying that the Central Government is now treating the Northeast issue as the biggest issue at present, with the greatest determination and the greatest sacrifice, vowing to unite and recover the eastern provinces. Zhang and Wu gave many speeches, and the representatives asked for a report on the Shanghai consultation process, which Wu also answered, saying that it has now been successfully concluded. The representatives were all satisfied. At 3 pm, the entire group went to the Military Officer School to petition Chiang, who personally met with them and gave a speech, saying that the government sincerely accepts the points requested by the people of the Northeast. Regarding the Northeast students who have no schools to return to, I have already talked to Principal Feng about finding ways to enable them to study and fulfill their ambitions and responsibilities. The government is also finding ways to provide relief to the displaced people of the Northeast. After Chiang finished speaking, Gao Jianguo, a representative of the delegation, asked the government about its diplomatic policy towards Japan. Chiang gave a satisfactory answer. It was not until 5:30 pm that they returned to Jinling University in formation. At 8 pm, Chiang summoned the representatives of the delegation's headquarters, 12 people in total, inquired about everything, and explained the government's diplomatic policy towards Japan in detail. The discussion lasted about an hour before they left. The delegation is now scheduled to petition the Fourth National Congress again on the morning of the 12th, pay their respects to the mausoleum in the afternoon, and return to Beiping to report on the evening of the 11th.

Special Telegram)

Peking University Students Petition Zhang Xueliang

(Beiping) More than 600 Peking University students petitioned Deputy Commander Zhang this morning, demanding (1) that the Japanese be stopped from causing disturbances and that he be responsible for protecting the soil and defending the people, (2) that firearms be issued, and (3) that war be declared on Japan. Zhang personally came out to meet them. (Special telegram, 10th)

Zhou Yawei's Opinion on Conscription

(Nanjing) Zhou Yawei told reporters yesterday that with the violent Japanese invasion and the national crisis becoming increasingly urgent, the government, in addition to striving for unity to jointly resist foreign aggression, should pay more attention to the military training of the people, so as to cultivate a sound physique as a preliminary step in implementing conscription. Zhou said that it is not easy to implement a conscription system in China, which has a vast territory and a large population, and it cannot be proportionally compared with other countries. Countries such as Japan, France, and Italy are implementing conscription systems because they have been implemented for a long time, and their territories are narrow and their populations are small, so they do not feel any difficulties. China is different due to its national conditions, and it should be discussed separately. Even the current conscription system in the country, the soldiers recruited are all children of poor families, relying on monthly salaries to support their families. If a conscription system is implemented, the soldiers will all be obligatory in nature. If a family has several members relying on them for a living, and they are conscripted into the army, the whole family will have no means of living. According to the actual total number of soldiers currently recruited, there are about two million in the country. If the country is unified, with this number of soldiers, plus appropriate training and cultivation, it is sufficient to defend the country. This is my humble opinion, but the government has already made a decision on conscription. After all parties have considered it thoroughly, if it is implemented and is indeed beneficial to the country, then it should be implemented sooner or later. (Special telegram, 11th)

Students from Harbin Go to Heilongjiang to Join the Army

(Harbin) Chen Difei, Min Jiaju, and Wen Yansheng, students from Harbin Normal School, wrote a letter to their classmates to join the army in Heilongjiang, angered by the Japanese army's atrocities. The travel expenses were dozens of yuan collected by pawning classmates' clothes. (Special telegram, 11th)

(Harbin) Nan Zhengshan and two other students from Harbin No. 1 Industrial School, all aged fourteen or fifteen, secretly went to Heilongjiang to join the army today. (Special telegram, 10th)

Envoys from various countries have dispatched personnel to investigate the truth of the incident, and warned the Japanese side to pay attention to the safety of Tianjin. I will stay in Beijing for a short while, then visit Chairman Jiang and attend the Special Foreign Affairs Committee to report on the truth of the Tianjin Incident. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Central Government Issues Circular Telegram to Achieve Unity

(Nanjing) The Central Executive Committee's Provisional Plenary Session passed and issued a circular telegram on the 11th to achieve unity. The original text is as follows:

Our party adheres to the late Premier's teachings and is committed to the National Revolution, aiming to advocate that the Chinese people practice the Three Principles of the People and place China in a realm of freedom and equality. In terms of revolutionary responsibility, all comrades should prioritize sacrifice and struggle for the sake of the country. In terms of revolutionary objectives, the party's interests should prioritize the nation's welfare. This year, banditry has not been quelled, and major disasters have followed one after another, causing death and displacement, and the people cannot bear it. Unprecedented foreign insults are taking advantage of the situation to achieve their goals. The country's affairs are in dire straits, like a pile of eggs. For several years, the Central Government has embodied the late Premier's teachings of love and sincerity towards the party, and has waited patiently for the comrades to realize the situation. Lately, it has become increasingly clear that national difficulties cannot be relieved without unity, and unity cannot be achieved without compromise. If the party and the country cease to exist, what is the point of disagreements? After repeated consultations, there is consensus. All party comrades are willing to understand and forgive each other, to eliminate the pain of disintegration, and to end the difficult situation of the past with the Fourth National Congress, establishing a foundation for the party's unity. We deeply believe that the late Premier's great spirit will illuminate, and with the guarantee of more than forty years of revolutionary history, all our party comrades will be able to sincerely consider the nation's difficulties, examine the revolutionary environment, follow the late Premier's teachings, and abide by the party's constitution, to fulfill the public's will and seek unified solidarity. From now on, with one heart and one mind, we will be loyal and courageous, resisting external aggression and relieving internal suffering. This is how our party will serve the people of the country. We hope that all compatriots and party comrades will understand this intention and work together. We respectfully report this matter for your joint consideration. The Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang. (Eleventh Dispatch)

The Venue for the Fourth National Congress is Completed; Memorial Week for the Premier's Birthday Will Be Followed by the Opening Ceremony of the Congress

(Nanjing) As of the afternoon of the 11th, more than 310 delegates to the Fourth National Congress had registered at the secretariat. A memorial service for the Premier's birthday will be held at the Central University Auditorium at 9 AM on the 12th, followed by the opening ceremony at 10 AM. The venue is ready. The seating arrangement for the delegates is semi-circular, with over 600 seats for delegates and observers. A portrait of the Premier is hung on the stage, along with photographic reproductions of the Premier's handwriting when he founded the Tongmenghui and reorganized the Chinese Revolutionary Party. The front row is for delegate speeches and the secretariat. The middle row is for the chair and secretaries, and the back row is for the presidium. A stenography table is located below the stage. Dozens of pots of fine chrysanthemums are placed on both sides of the stage, with no other decorations. No slogans are posted in the venue. A pine and cypress archway has been erected at the entrance of Central University, inscribed with the fourteen characters "Fourth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang," with a couplet beside it reading "Review the past work of political tutelage, establish the future scale of democracy." (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) All delegates to the Fourth National Congress and members of the Central Committee are scheduled to gather at the venue at 7 AM on the morning of the 13th to pay respects at the Premier's mausoleum. At 9 AM, a preparatory meeting will be held to arrange seating and ratify the rules of procedure for the Congress and the organizational regulations of the secretariat. The first formal meeting is scheduled for the morning of the 14th. The congress is expected to last for seven days, but no more than ten days at the latest. The proposals submitted by the delegates are being sorted by the secretariat. The content tends toward peaceful unification, diplomacy with Japan, and national defense issues. In essence, they are aimed at internal stability and external resistance, and their methods are similar. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The issue of the release of Deng Yanda, leader of the Third Party, will be submitted to the Fourth National Congress for discussion. (Eleventh Dispatch)

The National Government Establishes the Organizational Outline and List of Members of the Finance Committee

(Nanjing) The Provisional Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee on the 11th approved the organizational outline and list of members of the Finance Committee as follows:

Organizational Outline: Article 1: The National Government establishes a Finance Committee to review various income and expenditures of the national treasury and implement financial transparency. Article 2: The committee will have one chairman, to be filled by the President of the Executive Yuan, and 26 to 30 members, to be filled by government personnel, figures from the financial and industrial sectors, economists, and experts with relevant experience. Article 3: The functions of the committee are: (1) to reorganize finances; (2) to review the budgets of military and administrative expenses; (3) to audit the issuance of public bonds; (4) to assess and publicize income and expenditure figures. Article 4: The committee will hold meetings every two weeks, convened by the chairman. Article 5: At each meeting, the Ministry of Finance shall submit a report on the income and expenditure of the previous two weeks to the committee for review. Article 6: The committee will establish a secretariat, whose organization will be determined separately. Article 7: The detailed rules of procedure of the committee will be determined separately. Article 8: This outline shall be promulgated and implemented by the National Government.

List of Members (Government): Jiang Zhongzheng, Lin Sen, Yu Youren, Song Ziwen, He Yingqin, Li Yuying, Shao Yuanchong, Zhang Xueliang, Xu Yongchang, Han Fuqu. (Industry and Commerce): Rong Zongjing, Liu Hongsheng, Fan Xudong, Yu Hede. (Finance): Zhang Gongquan, Li Fuchun, Wu Daquan, Zhou Zuomin. (Academics): Gu Mengyu, Hu Shi, Ma Yinchu, Zhu Jiahua, Yang Quan. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Promulgation of the Organizational Outline of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Headquarters; Government Order Specially Appoints Chen Mingshu as Commander-in-Chief; Deployment of Defenses in the Two Regions is Under Detailed Planning

(Nanjing) The National Government issued an order on the 11th announcing the organizational outline of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief Headquarters. All previous titles of Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander should be abolished immediately. This order also specially appointed Chen Mingshu as the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief. This order also ordered the promulgation of the organizational outline of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief Headquarters. The organizational outline is as follows: (1) To maintain security in the capital and the area between Shanghai and Songhu, a Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief is specially established, to be specially appointed by the National Government. (2) The organization of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief Headquarters will be determined separately. (3) Within the area under his jurisdiction, if the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief encounters military or disaster-related events, he should immediately direct the subordinate units or consult with nearby garrison troops in the area to deal with the situation as appropriate. In urgent situations, he may petition the National Government to allow the use of martial law and immediately implement martial law. (4) When martial law is in effect, the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison Commander-in-Chief shall exercise his powers in accordance with the provisions of the martial law regulations. However, if martial law is not in effect, but he believes that the local situation requires the implementation of certain provisions of the martial law regulations, he may petition the National Government for approval to implement them. (5) This outline shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Eleventh Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After the conclusion of the Peace and Unification Conference, the inauguration of Chen Mingshu as Commander-in-Chief of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison has not yet been scheduled. It is said that the various units under the Nineteenth Route Army have not yet fully arrived in Beijing and Shanghai, and the allocation of troops along the railway lines is still being planned. Although the organizational outline of the General Headquarters has been promulgated, the responsibility for garrisoning and guarding Beijing and Shanghai is extremely important, and the allocation of troops stationed along the railway lines requires particularly careful planning in order to be properly implemented. Therefore, yesterday and today, Chen Mingshu specially invited Cai Tingkai, Mao Weishou, Yang Jianping, Chen Peikun, Ouyang Ju, and others to his residence to discuss everything. Once all the plans have been decided, they will be submitted to Jiang for approval before implementation. Therefore, Chen's inauguration date will be at the earliest after the conclusion of the Fourth National Congress. (Eleventh Dispatch)

Franco-German Joint Committee to Meet in Paris Tomorrow; German Chancellor to Attend in Person

▲ Berlin, National Day 10: The Franco-German Joint Committee is now scheduled to hold its inaugural meeting in Paris this Friday. The German delegation will depart for France tomorrow. Chancellor Bruning is among the chief representatives. However, due to the heavy workload in the country, it is difficult for him to be absent. The German newspapers are quite delighted with the convening of the Franco-German Joint Committee, believing that the opportunity for cooperation between the two countries has arrived, and that from now on, they may be able to begin to engage in a path of construction.

Important News

Japanese Incite Tianjin Incident

▲Doihara Secretly Came to Tianjin to Collude

▲Thugs All Departed from the Japanese Concession

▲Arms and Ammunition Also Supplied by Japanese Barracks

A dispatch from Beiping states that since occupying Liaoning and Jilin, the Japanese army has sought to create a new situation in North China, eradicating Zhang Xueliang's power to achieve their goal of dominating the three northeastern provinces. This news has long been an open secret. Indeed, on the 3rd of this month, Doihara, accompanied by Jin Liang, arrived in Tianjin. Less than five days later, the Tianjin Incident occurred. Upon learning of this, the reporter took a train to Tianjin at 11:00 AM on the 9th to conduct an on-the-ground investigation and returned to Beiping at 12:00 AM that night. The findings of the investigation are reported as follows:

After Doihara and Jin Liang arrived in Tianjin, Jin Liang's sole mission was to persuade Puyi to return to Shenyang and establish his so-called Ming Guang Empire. Doihara, in addition to jointly inducing and threatening Puyi with Jin Liang, had another major task: to unite pro-Japanese factions and seek to create a new situation in North China. Jin Liang's whereabouts were secretive. He lived at No. 93 Xinhua Li Li in the French Concession. [Tianjin City Area Map]

He also established a secret agency at the Beiyang Hotel in the Japanese Concession. He visited Puyi several times, repeatedly requesting him to return to Shenyang to restore the dynasty, presenting his so-called Emperor's Edict, stating that if he was willing to go out of the pass and organize the Ming Guang Empire, the Japanese Emperor would definitely provide full protection. Although some of his entourage echoed this, Puyi's father, Zaifeng, and the former officials Chen Baochen and Zheng Xiaoxu all firmly opposed it. Therefore, this matter has not been realized. As for Doihara, after arriving in Tianjin, he frequently associated with certain pro-Japanese leaders. After repeated discussions, it was decided that Zhang Bi and Li Jichun would come forward to establish a secret agency on Akiyama Street in the Japanese Concession, recruiting ruffians and secretly plotting an uprising. Zhang came from a background as a ruffian, and was previously the police commissioner during Feng Yuxiang's era, with many former subordinates. Li, on the other hand, was a Muslim with many desperate men under his command. At 8:00 PM on the 8th, everything was planned at the Akiyama Street agency, with great activity. The disaster struck at 11:45 PM.

The plainclothes teams recruited by Zhang Bi, Li Jichun, etc., numbered over 2,000, divided into groups of 30, each group with two Japanese soldiers directing them. Each person was paid four yuan per day, and the group leader was paid ten yuan. The Public Security Bureau's detectives had long detected these recruited plainclothes teams. Therefore, the authorities were fully aware of their every move. Wang Shu-chang, Chairman of Hebei Province, notified the consuls of various countries stationed in Tianjin on the 6th, stating that according to reports, there were reactionary elements secretly plotting to disrupt the security of Tianjin, and requesting that the consuls of various countries pay attention. At the same time, he notified the Japanese consul, informing him that there were reactionary elements hiding in the Japanese Concession, secretly plotting to disrupt security, and requesting that the undesirable elements in the Concession be strictly dealt with. After receiving the notifications, the consuls all said that they feared it was a rumor and not worth believing. By the 8th, the rumors became more intense. At 5:00 PM, Yao Dongfan of the 15th Brigade of the Northeast Army, acting on emergency orders, arrived from Junliangcheng and deployed sentries outside the XinZhan Railway Station to inspect pedestrians. They then advanced to the station and later guarded Dajing Road. The merchants and people of Tianjin all thought that some important person was coming to Tianjin, so the military and police were on high alert. At 6:00 PM, the Hebei police also added double posts, all the military police were dispatched, and the security team's bicycle teams continued to depart. All entertainment venues in the city, such as cinemas, theaters, acrobatics halls, and miscellaneous places, were ordered to stop night operations. At about 7:00 PM, martial law was simultaneously announced on various roads in BeidaGuan, Nankai, Hedong, and the walled city. At 9:00 PM, all streetcars were ordered to enter the depot. Police informed merchants and residents to close their doors and sleep soundly. At this point, the citizens began to realize that an incident had occurred and were greatly alarmed. At the same time, Japanese soldiers also armed themselves and sealed off the intersections on the border between China and Japan, setting up barbed wire, only allowing pedestrians to go out but not to enter. They also informed merchants and residents to close their doors. At about 10:00 PM, more than 300 plainclothes team members in the Zha Kou area of ​​the Japanese Concession were preparing to attack the Public Security Bureau. At the same time, more than 1,000 plainclothes team members arrived at the Japanese barracks in Haiguang Temple from Penglai Street in the Japanese Concession and received guns and ammunition from the Japanese. They originally intended to attack the Public Security Bureau fiercely from the Zha Kou area, but because the Public Security Bureau was heavily guarded, they changed their plan. The first route passed through the Qiangzi River from Haiguang Temple, entered the southern city, entered the South Gate, exited the East Gate, and attacked the rear of the Public Security Bureau. The second route attacked the front of the Public Security Bureau from Zha Kou. The third route was ambushed in Hebei in advance, attempting to occupy the provincial and municipal governments and the headquarters of the Second Army after the uprising. At 10:55 PM, the first route began to attack the first district and the second precinct. The police at the precinct, because the precinct was close to the Japanese barracks, did not fire back. The second route began to attack from Zha Kou at the same time. The third route had not yet taken action. At 11:30 PM, more than 100 plainclothes team members attacked Dongma Road from the north entrance of Asahi Street in the Japanese Concession. More than a dozen Japanese soldiers behind them set up machine guns and swept across Dongma Road. At the same time, 60 to 70 plainclothes team members attacked the first district and the sixth precinct from Luzhuangzi. The police at the precinct also did not retaliate because the precinct was close to the Japanese Concession. After 12:00 AM, the first route occupied the first district and the second precinct from Haiguang Temple and then continued to attack. The plainclothes team members advanced to the Xinhua Bridge on the Chinese Merchants' Racecourse and were captured alive by the security team, more than a dozen of them. When the first route attacked, there were two Japanese armored vehicles following in front, and two Japanese officers were directing. As for the second route, when the plainclothes team members attacked from Zha Kou to the vicinity of the Second Telephone Bureau, they were captured alive by the security team, more than a dozen of them. Because the area was under fire, there were many stray bullets flying around, and all the glass windows were broken, but fortunately no one was injured. The plainclothes team failed to attack Dongma Road from the north entrance of Asahi Street, and more than a dozen people sneaked into the

Page 9

Hucao An alley, intending to attack Dongmenlian from there. Because there were police ambushed there in advance, they were also captured alive. Another group of more than a dozen plainclothes team members retreated to Ximenlian and encountered an armored car of the Public Security Bureau driving by, so they threw a grenade, and the car was slightly damaged. These more than a dozen plainclothes team members were also all captured alive. The captain of the security team, Shang, was injured. At 1:00 AM on the 9th, Wang Shu-chang notified the consuls of various countries by telephone, saying that an unfortunate incident had now occurred. More than 1,000 rioters attacked the Chinese area in several routes. In order to respect the Sino-British Treaty, our country did not retaliate. Please inform the Japanese consul to prevent the rioters from retreating into the Japanese border at dawn, and please expel the rioters from the Japanese Concession. At 3:00 AM, the consuls of the United States, France, Britain, Germany, and Italy held a meeting at the American consulate. The consuls all expressed their deep sympathy to the Chinese authorities for this unfortunate incident. It was decided to notify the Japanese consul to respect the spirit of the Sino-British Treaty and ban undesirable elements from entering the concession. The Chinese authorities believed that with this method, our country could capture more than 2,000 plainclothes team members alive without firing a shot. However, at about 5:00 AM, the Japanese Tianjin Garrison Headquarters suddenly protested to the Second Army Headquarters by telephone, saying that a platoon leader of the Japanese army had been shot and killed by Chinese soldiers while on duty to prevent rioters from invading the Japanese Concession. Now, Chinese police are ordered to retreat 300 meters immediately, otherwise, the Japanese army will take free measures when necessary. Wang asked, if the Chinese police withdrew, who would be responsible for the security within the 300 meters? And what is the reason why they must retreat? The Japanese army headquarters actually replied that after the Chinese police withdraw, the Japanese side can be responsible for maintaining security, and there is no need to explain the reason for the retreat, etc. The arrogance of the tone can be seen from this. Wang sternly refused. Unexpectedly, another phone call came soon, still ordering the Chinese police to retreat and limiting it to before 6 o'clock. Wang, in view of the situation at the time, in order to avoid conflict and clarify responsibility, ordered the security team to temporarily retreat. Who would have thought that when the security team retreated, the plainclothes team would launch a fierce attack, intending to take advantage of this period, under the cover of the Japanese army, to retreat into the Japanese Concession. At 6:30 AM, the second route made no progress in the attack. The Japanese army began to use artillery to bombard the Public Security Bureau. From 6:30 AM to 7:00 AM, 14 artillery shells were fired. After 7:00 AM, there were still sporadic shots. One of the shells destroyed the office building of the Second Telephone Bureau and killed two coachmen on the road. The rest fell into the Dongluo Bridge River. The sound of artillery gradually subsided until 7:30 AM. It was already dawn. Wang Shu-chang then questioned the Japanese consul again, asking why he bombarded with artillery. Unexpectedly, the Japanese consul did not reply at first. It took half an hour before he shirked responsibility, saying that it was not fired by the Japanese army. However, at that time, there were many Italian sailors on the opposite bank of Zha Kou. Seeing that the artillery fire came from the Japanese barracks, they were all willing to be witnesses to prove that the artillery was fired by the Japanese army.

When the incident occurred, all the Japanese troops in the Japanese Concession were dispatched, firing guns arbitrarily in the Concession. The injured in the Concession were all sent to Kyouritsu Hospital. One person died in front of the Great North Hotel, and one person was injured behind the Four-Sided Clock. It is not yet known whether there were any casualties among the citizens in other places. At about 11:00 PM on the 8th, Japanese soldiers along the river in the Japanese Concession fired machine guns and rifles at Special District 2 and prepared several boats along the river, intending to occupy the river as soon as the Chinese police returned fire. However, the Chinese police did not return fire from beginning to end, so the Japanese army disturbed each other all night and had no excuse. Japanese Consul Goto then telegraphed the Chinese authorities, saying, "At 10:00 PM last night, more than 1,000 rioters were found in Balitai, with the potential to enter the Japanese Concession. The Japanese army had no choice but to dispatch urgently and take legitimate defense." At the same time, he used radio to ask the Lushun fleet to send warships to Tianjin as soon as possible to protect overseas Chinese. As for the Japanese Garrison Headquarters, it had transported more than 20 boxes of munitions to the Japanese barracks from Tanggu on the evening of the 7th. On the 8th, it issued two more orders: (1) Order veterans to complete the organization within ten hours; (2) Establish a wartime hospital in the Japanese Flower Garden Auditorium. The intention is clear. As for the French Concession, after the Japanese army sealed off the intersections on the border between China and Japan when the incident occurred, it also sent patrols to guard the border between France and Japan. After the sound of gunfire, the French Concession Board of Directors immediately dispatched armored vehicles to Xikai for alert and sent Annam soldiers to guard the Wanguo Bridge. At 1:30 AM, the middle section of the Wanguo Bridge was moved away. Although the British Concession was slightly less guarded, all patrol officers were on patrol. On that night, due to the sudden incident, the men and women who were entertained in the play areas of the British and French concessions who could not return to the Japanese Concession and various places in the Hebei Special Zone had to open rooms in hotels and hotels for the night. Therefore, there was a shortage of people in large and small hotels, and there were also those who stayed in brothels and dark prostitutes' homes, which was a situation where they were overwhelmed on Shanyin Road. And there were no less than 6,000 rickshaws gathered in the British and French concessions from the Japanese Concession and other places. Both sides of the main streets were crowded with rickshaws, as if there was a rickshaw exhibition.

After the reporter finished the investigation, he went to the Provincial and Municipal Government to visit Wang Shuchang and Zhang Xueming. He first went to the Municipal Government. According to Zhang Xueming, the mastermind behind the Tianjin riot of the reactionary elements has been clearly told to us by the facts. I don’t need to explain it. However, regarding the security of Tianjin, I am determined to maintain it with all my strength. There are now more than 1,800 security team members in Tianjin who have received more than ten years of military education. I believe that if there are no Japanese secretly plotting among the plainclothes team members, the security team will have the ability to eliminate them. When the riot started last night, more than 3,000 troops were ordered to open outside the city within three hours, but because they respected the Sino-British Treaty, they did not order them to open into the city. They will never order the troops to open into the city to maintain security unless it is absolutely necessary. After meeting Wang Shuchang, Wang said that three days before the incident, I notified the consuls of various countries stationed in Tianjin of the unstable news I had obtained. When the incident occurred, I also notified the consuls. Today, the Tianjin Municipal Government has a protest letter to the Japanese consul in Tianjin. I believe that the security of Tianjin is extremely solid. On the Beiping side, after Zhang, the Deputy Commander, received the alarm on the night of the 8th, he ordered Wang Shuchang and Zhang Xueming to strengthen their defense and handle it carefully. On the morning of the 9th, he sent his adjutant, Ji Yitian, with two machine guns, to Tianjin by special train from Ping and arrived at 9:00 AM. He went to visit Wang Shuchang and conveyed the Deputy Commander's order, ordering Wang to be fully responsible for maintaining the security of Tianjin. The Tianjin authorities announced martial law on the 9th. Here is the original text of the announcement: "To announce the matter, at 10:00 PM on the 8th of this month, a reactionary plainclothes team of about 1,000 people was found in the Zha Kou area, attempting to attack the various sub-bureaus of the city's public security. After reporting to the Chairman, it was decided to implement the announcement of martial law in accordance with the martial law regulations from the 9th of this month. If there are any unruly people who intend to cause disturbance, they will be arrested and dealt with by military law. The people of the city should also live in peace and not disturb them without authorization. This is extremely important. This announcement is made for everyone to know. Tianjin Mayor Zhang Xueming." (Morning of the 10th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Xu Yabo Welcomes and Returns Xu Yabo, the former chief of the First Water Police District of Songjiang, was suspected of colluding with Tai Bao A Shu in Shanghai. He was captured by the First Water Police District and escorted by the Police Department to the First Court of the Special Zone for interrogation. The County Court of this county previously, based on the XinZhuang Xu's robbery case, seized a passbook. Later, it was discovered that Xu Yabo had sent someone to the bank to collect the passbook, and he was suspected of being a common accomplice in this case. The court had previously prepared a document to welcome and return to Shanghai. Xu Yabo filed an appeal against the transfer and punishment. The appeal was rejected by the Higher Court. He was welcomed and returned to Songjiang from Shanghai at 6:00 PM yesterday (10th). He was interrogated by the prosecutor that night and was found to be suspected of being a common thief, and a lawsuit was filed with the court for trial.

The Hengchang Bank Robbery Case in Fengjing was solved. The case of the Hengchang Bank in Fengjing being robbed of more than 3,000 yuan of banknotes and foreign currency on the evening of the 8th has now been solved. A former partner of the Yuzhenyu Store, Yongguan, will be sent to court.

Suzhou

The Water Police Rescued the Abducted Passengers of the Feiyun Wheel. Due to the rampant lake bandits recently, the Water Police of the Second and Third Districts of Suxi have dispatched teams to search and suppress them in all directions. On the 10th of this month, the Water Police encountered several bandit ships in the Maji Mountain area of Shuili Lake, with 70 to 80 bandits. The two sides opened fire for dozens of minutes, and the bandits fled. When the fire was opened, two abducted passengers, Yan Jisheng and Ye Fenglin, escaped. They were kidnapped by bandits from the Feiyun Small Wheel a few days ago. Yan Jisheng was priced at 100,000 yuan for ransom. The two abducted passengers have now arrived in Wuxi. According to the villagers in the Maji Mountain area, there are still four or five female passengers abducted from the Feiyun Wheel among the bandits, including one pregnant woman, who is the daughter-in-law of Chu. Shen, the district chief, has sent telegrams to various teams to quickly pursue and suppress them. It is also reported that the Water Police have captured three bandits, Wang Deming, Wu Xueyi, and Xiong Chunshan, in the South Taihu area, and they were escorted to Suzhou yesterday (11th).

Wuxi

Instructors of the Volunteer Army Arrive in Xishi Provincial Wuxi Middle School, and the College of Education, Private Wuxi Middle School, Furen Middle School, and Guoxue College have organized youth volunteer armies one after another since the Shenyang incident and submitted them

Approved by the Central Training Headquarters, Xu Jiande (Guangdong), a student of the advanced class of the Central Military Academy, was appointed as the instructor of the Provincial Xizhong, Li Qichao (Guangdong) as the instructor of Guozhuan, Qin Tian (Sichuan) as the instructor of Private Xizhong, Zhao Shuyou (Hunan) as the instructor of Furen Middle School, and Ouyang Geng (Guangxi) as the instructor of the Provincial College of Education. They arrived in Xishi together yesterday and went to the designated schools to serve. They also discussed with the principals of each school and planned to organize a military training committee in each school, with the principal, all levels of grade heads, and instructors as members. All military affairs of the Youth Volunteer Army of the whole school are under the management of the committee. As for the organization, each 50 people is a district team, which is divided into several classes, 300 to 600 people is a large team, and 600 to 1,200 people is a column. Six people share one gun. The Central Government has ordered the Shanghai Arsenal to rush to manufacture them. Once they are manufactured, they will be verified and issued by the General Headquarters.

The Fifth District Robbed Seven Families The Zhu Lane near Tangtou Town in the Fifth District of the county was robbed by more than a dozen bandits at about 1:00 AM on the 9th, carrying pistols, wooden sticks, and flashlights. They first went to Xie Ruisheng's house in Xiexing Village to rob, then to Yang PanGen's house, and finally to Zhu Qinan, Zhu Sanyuan, Zhu Xiangbao, Zhu Zhonggeng, and Zhu Lixing's houses in Zhu Lane, totaling seven houses. It lasted three hours. Alarm gongs rang everywhere, and the bandits took the loot and left. Most of the robbed households were poor, so the losses were not large.

Qingjiang

The Bandits in Guanmen Town Burned and Killed. There is a place called Guanmen Town outside the South Gate of Huaiyin, which is only seven or eight miles away from the county town. There is a large Liu family manor there, with more than a dozen households. At about 10:00 PM on the 5th, more than 40 bandits suddenly went from the northwest, first to Liu Dianbiao's house and knocked on the door. Liu Dianbiao's house opened a soil cannon and killed a bandit and injured five or six bandits, which aroused the anger of the bandits. They burned every house they encountered and killed anyone they encountered, causing the houses of nine families, including Liu Dianbiao, Liu Dianjun, Liu Chaoju, Liu Zhaorui, Liu Dianfang, Zhang Xuedao, Zhang Xueqin, Luo Bingfu, and Luo Wanshun, to be burned down, totaling 40 to 50 houses. Liu Dianbiao's second son, Zhaofu, eldest daughter-in-law, Wang, second daughter-in-law, Ma, and granddaughter, Xiaoguiniang, were burned to death, and a hired worker, Li Jinwen, was killed, as well as Liu Chaoju's mother, Sun, and Liu Dianbiao and his eldest son, Zhaogan, were seriously injured. In addition, more than a dozen livestock, such as donkeys, cattle, and pigs, were burned to death. As for the clothes, food, and items of each family, as well as the title deeds of the fields and houses, there was nothing left. This is indeed a massive robbery that has not been seen in the recent city in recent years.

Important News

The Ministry of Education Commends the Department of Education of the Eastern Provinces Special Zone for Caring about Social Education

▲Adding Specialties and Increasing Funding for Social Education This Year

According to the report of the Department of Education of the Eastern Provinces Special Zone to the Ministry of Education, the previous instructions stipulated that the third point of the key items for promoting social education and paying attention to them should be to set up a specialty for managing social education. Because the budget of this department is severely limited, the organization cannot be changed suddenly. Therefore, a Public Education Committee has been temporarily established to specialize in its affairs. The Ministry has approved the temporary flexible handling, and a specialty will be set up after the budget is increased. Now, because of the previous reasons, the Public Education Committee has been canceled from this year and the Fifth Section has been established to specialize in social education administration, so as to effectively promote social education and be solely responsible. Moreover, the education funding for the 20th year of the Republic of China has increased by more than 146,000 yuan compared with the 19th year, among which the new education funding item has increased by 33,000 yuan for the public education hall and 13,000 yuan for the museum under the Cultural Relics Research Institute, totaling 46,000 yuan, accounting for about 35% of the total increase in funding. The situation of adding social education specialties and increasing social education funding will be presented for review and record, etc. The Ministry of Education instructed that the report has been received. In order to promote social education, the department has followed the order to set up a specialty for managing social education administration from this year and allocated 35% of the newly increased education funding this year to social education. This is a sign of active progress and is deeply commendable. The request for record should be approved.

Military Training Implemented in Hunan's Senior High Schools

Changsha Dispatch: The Hunan provincial government has decided to implement military training in senior high schools and above. Regulations have already been drafted and circulated for implementation. However, the regulations regarding the training director, training officers, and military teaching assistants are determined by the General Headquarters through examination. Seventeen training directors, fifty-one training officers, and one hundred and fifty-eight teaching assistants have now been selected. According to the number of students receiving military training in each school, one military teaching assistant is assigned to each group of twenty students, and one military training officer is assigned to every three groups. For schools with more than one hundred students, one military training director is assigned. For schools with fewer than one hundred students, one military training director兼training officer is assigned. Assignments have been made in detail according to these standards. As for the monthly salaries, subsidies, and expenses of the personnel, in addition to the funds that each school should provide, any shortfall will be subsidized by the General Headquarters to ease the burden on each school. The names of the assigned personnel are as follows: (1) Hunan University: Military Training Director Cao Mu, Training Officers Xia Boying, Hu Ming, Xu Wujie, Zhu Sixun, Huang Dianmo, Cao Hui, Zhao Jiazhuo, Ji Longbin, Chen Guonan; (2) First High School: Military Training Director Tang Ce, Training Officers Tan Ruzhen, He Zhenguo, Wang Lixing, Zhao Tiecheng, Deng Jianhou, Shi Jingchuan, Liu Pingfan, Zhu Kai; (3) Senior Vocational School: Military Training Director Ouyang Li, Training Officers Xiao Zan, Zhang Shiwen, Zhou Shengyu, Song Boqi; (4) Senior Agricultural School: Military Training Director Lei Shiqing, Training Officers Zeng Qingxun, Zhang Youxun, Hu Lixian, Li Tianzhu; (5) First Normal School: Military Training Director Jiang Bao'san, Training Officers Shen He'san, Huang Dacai, Lei Fengheng, Sheng Zexiong, Shao Jiuwu, Liu Shizhu; (6) Xiangya Medical College: Military Training Director Tan Mianze; (7) Mingde School: Military Training Director Wu Fen'cun, Training Officers Yang Fengxian, Li Chengxun, Zhang Pengzhu; (8) Miaogaofeng School: Military Training Director Tang Junmian; (9) Yueyun School: Military Training Director Kuang Shushu, Training Officers Li Dapeng, Sun Baosheng, Huang Xizhang; (10) Chuyi School: Military Training Director Zhang Tiexiang, Training Officers Tian Jie, Zheng Yan; (11) Guangyi School: Military Training Director Zhou Dahua, Training Officers Zeng Shufan, Xu Ying; (12) Dalv School: Military Training Director Hu Zaikun, Training Officers Zheng Wuchen, Cao Guodong; (13) Qunyi School: Military Training Director Zhong Weiqun, Training Officers Jiang Xiong, Cao Xudong, Shi Qi, Huang Zhichun; (14) Wenyi School: Military Training Director Hou Yejing, Training Officers Su Liang, Tan Fanshu; (15) Yali School: Military Training Director Liu Wendong; (16) Huazhong School: Military Training Director Ma Shutang, Training Officers Li Ying, Peng Difei; (17) Changjun School: Military Training Director He Ying.

Zhejiang Education Department Stipulates Specified Work for Educational Institutions

▲ Now Issued to All Counties and Cities for Compliance

The Zhejiang Education Department believes that the local education guidance organization in the province this year has expanded its scope due to practical needs, and the guidance work should be intensified to achieve practical results. Recently, it has specially formulated a type of specified work for educational institutions at all levels in the 20th year of the Republic, and ordered all counties and cities to comply with and earnestly implement it. Excerpts are as follows:

(A) Regarding the Education Department: (1) Provincial inspectors and specialized supervisors should formulate appropriate inspection plans; (2) Organize a provincial local education guidance committee; (3) Pay attention to guiding the implementation of national salvation education; (4) Hold the Second Provincial Education Achievement Exhibition; (5) Expand the Provincial Education Achievement Exhibition Hall into a Provincial Education Achievement Reference Room; (6) Appropriately expand the correspondence research department for teacher training improvement based on existing undertakings; (7) Hold vacation workshops by region; (8) Formulate standards and points for attention for counties and cities in handling various social education methods; (9) Compile and print publications for guiding mass education; (10) Collect and introduce various social education publications and materials and methods for implementing mass education; (11) Contact construction agencies, autonomous agencies, and vocational education institutions in the province to implement livelihood education and promote local autonomy; (12) Guide designated local and mass education experimental areas.

(B) Regarding the counties and cities: (1) County and city inspectors, supervisors, and district education officers should formulate inspection plans; (2) Within three months of the beginning of the year, organize and establish a county and city school district guidance conference; (3) Prepare to establish central primary schools and central mass schools; for those already established, try to enrich their content; (4) Various institutions within the county and city responsible for guidance work should formulate guidance plans and guidance records; (5) Try to hold educational demonstrations, achievement exhibitions, painting tours, outbound visits, meetings, lectures, and other activities; (6) Set up a primary education reference room or a circulating library; (7) Hold primary school graduation exams; (8) Formulate measures to improve private primary schools and private schools; (9) Each primary school should recruit enough students; (10) Set up special courses or full-time staff members to handle social education; (11) Formulate measures to improve mass education centers, mass learning nuclei, and other existing social education undertakings; (12) Improve various social education statistics.

Youth Volunteer Army of Various Universities Reviewed in the Wind and Rain in the Fourth District

▲ Over 2,000 Youth Volunteers from Schools Including Sino-French College Arrived

▲ Vowed to Use Iron Blood to Overthrow Japanese Imperialism

(Shanghai News Agency) The military training department of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of students from various universities in the city organized the periodic review of the youth volunteer army in different districts. The first, second, and third districts have been reviewed separately in the playgrounds of Fudan University, Jinda University, and Zhonggong University, respectively, with good results. Yesterday morning at 9 o'clock, the combined review of the third group in the fourth district was held at the Ximen Public Stadium. It was originally scheduled for fourteen schools to be reviewed. Except for Jiaotong University, Shanghai National Medical College, Shanghai Journalism College, Chinese Medical College, National Conservatory of Music, Datong University, and other schools that did not participate, the remaining schools braved the rain to assemble and await review, fully demonstrating the spirit that the youth volunteer army should possess. The review results were very satisfactory. The details are provided below by a reporter from the Shanghai News Agency:

▲ The inspected armies included 300 youth volunteers from the Sino-French Institute of Technology, 300+ from the School of Law and Politics, 30 female ambulance members, 100 from the Sino-French Pharmaceutical College, 10 female ambulance members, 400 from Aurora University, 400 from the Shanghai Art School, 40+ female ambulance members, 200 from Xinhua Art College, 50 female ambulance members, 200+ from Tongde Medical College, 100+ female ambulance members, 50+ from the East Asia Physical Education College, 20 male ambulance members with well-prepared tents and other rescue equipment, 200 from the Liangjiang Women's Volunteer Army, 100 female ambulance members, and over 10 other schools, totaling over 2,000 people. Except for the Tongde Medical College female ambulance members wearing white uniforms, the rest wore blue uniforms.

▲ Attendees for review: (1) Presidium: Wen Guangyi from the Military Department of the Student Union, Chen Yuejiang from the Sino-French Institute of Technology, Wang Yang from Aurora University; (2) Review Officers: Xiong Xuanwu, Zhong Dao, Qiu Jianmin, Chen Yinhua and others; (3) Representatives from the Sino-French Institute of Technology: Lin Zuhuan, Gu Lihua from Liangjiang; (4) Representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters: Yu Zhongbiao; (5) Commander-in-Chief: Cui Nanchang from the Sino-French Institute of Technology; (6) Masters of Ceremonies: Representatives from the Shanghai Art School, Recorder Li Zhiquan, Zhang Zhongbao.

▲ Order of the Review: (1) Review personnel take the stage (music played); (2) Commander-in-Chief reports the number of people; (3) Sing the party song; (4) Remove hats and pay the highest respect to the party's national flag and the portrait of the Premier, then put hats back on; (5) Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (6) Moment of silence (three minutes); (7) The commander maneuvers the teams to the designated review location to await inspection; (8) Review officer steps down to inspect; (9) After the review, the review officer goes on the stage and the commander issues a rest command; (10) Chairman reports; (11) Review personnel give instructions; (13) Music played; (14) Ceremony concludes.

▲ Circumstances of the Review: Despite the autumn wind and heavy rain and muddy ground, the troops from various schools demonstrated a spirit of fearlessness and waited for the review, which was truly commendable. The review began with a military parade. Due to the overly muddy ground, the originally planned divisional parade could not be held. Instead, each school took turns performing. The Sino-French Institute of Technology performed platoon drills. The whole army was orderly and spirited, and the various movements were very proficient. The Liangjiang Volunteer Army performed gun drills, and the ambulance team performed battlefield rescue, casualty carrying and various movements, which were also very agile. In the heavy rain and slippery ground, the spirit of the female compatriots to save the country was especially evident. Then a platoon from Aurora University performed changing formations, with commendable results.

▲ Wang Yang reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that all students should embrace the spirit of sacrifice, fight for national salvation, create everything with iron blood, and overthrow Japanese imperialism. Without military preparation, peace can never be realized. Therefore, armed national salvation cannot be delayed any longer.

▲ Chen Yuejiang reported on the preparations, stating that today was originally scheduled for the review of the second group in the fourth district. During the preparations, it was felt that the number of people in the separate reviews of the first and second groups in this district was too small. Therefore, it was decided through preparatory meetings to combine the two groups for a joint review today. Fifteen schools were supposed to attend today, but only ten schools with more than 2,000 people actually arrived due to rain or other reasons. However, the spirit and results were very good, and we are very satisfied with this.

▲ Wen Guangyi reported that today is a symbol of our hot blood and rain mixing together. In the future, I hope to have the opportunity to mix our blood and rain together to overthrow Japanese imperialism, and so on.

▲ Review Officer Wu Zhongdao instructed that we who are now soldiers should have the following conditions: (1) solemnity, (2) speed, (3) silence, (4) orderliness.

▲ Wu Baojin, the representative of the Student Union Military Training Department, said that in this period of wind and rain, armed students are able to participate without fear or timidity. This is the spirit of youth. In today's meeting place, the inferior roots of the Chinese nation have been washed clean. The significance of the review: (1) to show the spirit of the people, (2) to hope that the authorities do not rely on the League of Nations. It is hoped that the armed students of China will hold a general review of the youth volunteer army of all universities in Shanghai in the near future in preparation for overthrowing Japanese imperialism. Students in Shanghai should stand on the front line to fight.

▲ Yu Zhongbiao, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, read out the instructions: (1) have the determination to sacrifice, (2) avenge the country, (3) continue to maintain our spirit today. Finally, after each team shouted slogans, they separately formed up and returned to school with great spirits, showing no fear of the rain and wind.
